  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2311510210" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2311510210" />
    <a title="Laura Herondale" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/52844833-laura-herondale"><img alt="Laura Herondale" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1550655303p2/52844833.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2311510210?book_show_action=true">Sep 29, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Laura Herondale" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Laura Herondale" href="/user/show/52844833-laura-herondale">Laura Herondale</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781910655863" href="/book/show/29566743-under-rose-tainted-skies">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52844833-laura-herondale?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52844833-laura-herondale?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52844833-laura-herondale?shelf=mental-illness">mental-illness</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52844833-laura-herondale?shelf=read-in-2018">read-in-2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52844833-laura-herondale?shelf=4-5-stars">4-5-stars</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2311510210" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5727141323918878387">TW: OCD, agoraphobia, anxiety, depression, self harm. These are all prominent themes within the book, and will therefore be talked about in a fair amount of detail in this review. Please proceed with caution if any of these being portrayed in literature and/or being discussed is likely to trigger you. Take care <3<br/><br/>Also, note that throughout this review I will be heavily drawing from my own experiences with mental illness. For reference, I was diagnosed with Generalised Anxiety Disorder and Major </span>
  <span id="freeText5727141323918878387" style="display:none">TW: OCD, agoraphobia, anxiety, depression, self harm. These are all prominent themes within the book, and will therefore be talked about in a fair amount of detail in this review. Please proceed with caution if any of these being portrayed in literature and/or being discussed is likely to trigger you. Take care &lt;3<br /><br />Also, note that throughout this review I will be heavily drawing from my own experiences with mental illness. For reference, I was diagnosed with Generalised Anxiety Disorder and Major Depressive Disorder (now Persistent Depressive Disorder) when I was 15 (but started experiencing symptoms when I was 12), and self harmed regularly from the time I was 14 until around the time I turned 16, with a couple relapses when I was 16 (but I’ve been clean for 11 months now). I still have trouble talking about all this (more so the self harm than the depression and the anxiety, since I’ve talked about it a lot less, but still), so I might get a bit emotional and rambly. But I also can’t review books about mental illnesses without talking about my own experiences, as they shape my opinion on them so much. So yeah, bare with me.<br /><br /><b>Spoilers</b><br /><br />Ok, now onto the review. I dunno what I’d rate this if I could actually be objective about mental health books, but since, instead, I am complete trash for all of them (as long as the rep is good, obviously) this gets 4.5 stars. I did still have some problems with this book, but for the most part, I loved this.<br /><br />So I’ll start with Norah: I absolutely loved her. Her struggles with mental illness, specifically agoraphobia and OCD, were raw, realistic, and very relatable, and I adore this book because of that. I don’t have OCD or agoraphobia, so I can’t speak for the representation of these mental illnesses specifically (though this story is #ownvoices and I’ve heard it’s very good from people who do have these mental illnesses, so I believe the representation is accurate), but I do have an anxiety disorder, and I found myself consistently relating to the way Norah thought. And, over the course of the book, Norah developed symptoms of depression and self harmed, both of which I have experience with, and thus, related to quite a lot as well. I’ve been really into the whole “quoting half the book in order to show people what you’re on about instead of having to articulate your own thoughts through a bunch of long-ass paragraphs no one’s going to read” thing lately (I say ‘lately’, but I haven’t actually done it in a few months), so here’s a bunch of quotes that showcase how Norah’s mental illnesses manifest in her thoughts that I found to be very realistic and relatable (warning: I then proceed to write long-ass paragraphs about each quote, so was there really any point to this? No. But you should all be used to my ramblings by now):<br /><br /><i>“I have this thing about swallowing mind-altering medication...It’s the idea of relinquishing control that makes them too sticky to swallow.”</i><br /><br />Often times, anxiety is about needing control, and this book does such a good job of showing that, this being just one example. This was exactly how I felt when I was first given medication. I refused to take it for a long while, and continued to get worse mentally, and it was only after I had been in psychotherapy for a few months that I finally was able to feel comfortable enough to take it. Whilst I will always be a little uncomfortable with medication being portrayed negatively in a book, it’s a very realistic reaction, especially for people with anxiety, and by the end of this book Norah is taking her medication, having learned that it could be helpful, so I ended up really relating to this.<br /><br /><i>“It’s weird, the release I get from dragging the tiny metal arm across my skin...It’s drastic, a last resort. But so easy...One quick slice, where nobody can see, and it all stops. This is not about dying. This is about trying to get back some control.”</i><br /><br />Again, control. It’s the basis for so many mental illnesses, and this entire paragraph showcases just how desperate people with a mental illness can be to gain back even an ounce of it. I do want to mention that this is not the only reason that people self harm, but it is a big one. It was the primary reason that I used to. Even just carrying a blade with me used to make me feel safer, because I knew that if I did have a panic attack, I had that option. I had that last resort. And it was effective at stopping my panic attacks, back when I didn’t have other, safer techniques and methods to calm myself down in moments of intense anxiety. Plus, the way it was described in this book (although possibly triggering for some) was so raw and heartbreaking, but also just very real.<br /><br />What I really appreciated from this book was that Norah cut her thighs, rather than her wrists. Not only did this really resonate with me because I did the same, but I also appreciated this because, despite this being a very common place for people to self harm, most people don’t really know that. When people think of self harm, they tend to think of people cutting their wrists, but, in reality, there are many forms of self harm (which I’ll get into later), and there are many places on a person’s body where someone will harm themselves, the thighs being the second most common after the wrists/arms. And so this scene could also be quite educational for people who may not know much about self harm, and maybe help more people to spot it easier and quicker if their loved ones are harming themselves, and get them the help they need.<br /><br /><i>“...whether I like to admit it or not, anxiety has become my best friend. It’s a crutch that helps me hobble through life...I don’t know how to be safe without it.”</i><br /><br />This is so incredibly realistic, in my experience. When I first started experiencing my anxiety symptoms, I hated them. After a couple years, I still did. But I’d also become accustomed to my anxiety, and even began relying on it. Rather than doing something that may end up making me look stupid, or could be slightly dangerous or risky, I’d just avoid it all together, which meant that I never got hurt by anything. I relied on my anxiety to pull me away from anything that could go wrong, but it also meant that I pulled away from life itself.<br /><br />But when you start recovery for an anxiety disorder, you start doing things you stopped doing because they were too risky, and sometimes, things go wrong. You get hurt. You look stupid. You do something wrong. You lose control. And then you hate yourself for ever listening to anything but your anxiety, because look at what happened. Your anxiety kept you safe. And that’s such a massive hurdle to get over. One that takes years and years and you never completely do. Because it’s so easy to fall back into the habit of listening to your anxiety. It’s so easy to shut yourself away. But it’s not living. And this is something that, even after being in recovery for 2 years, I still struggle with daily.<br /><br />This is something that happens with a lot of other mental illnesses too, btw. Eating disorders, bipolar disorder, depressive disorders, etc all have elements to them that can lead to these mental illnesses becoming a sort of crutch for people, making one of the hardest steps in recovery being getting over this need to preserve your mental illness. And this is something that a lot of people who don’t have any experience with a mental illness can sometimes find quite confusing, because why would someone want to keep experiencing a mental illness? But I’m so incredibly grateful that this was included in this book, because it can be such a massive struggle, and I really related to this feeling, and found comfort in knowing that there was someone else experiencing the same thing (because sometimes even when you know there are other people experiencing the same symptoms as you, it’s still incredibly comforting to see it).<br /><br /><i>“...I can be hella frustrating...Fact of the matter is, people who depend on the level of perfection I do are tiring. It takes some getting used to, and it won’t ease up until I do.”</i><br /><br />I love this. This is the first book about mental illness ever that I’ve read that addresses this. At the end of the day, having a family member with a mental illness can be incredibly frustrating sometimes. Some days, I feel like I physically can’t get out of bed, and that can be really frustrating for my parents, who just want me to be able to go live my life and be happy. My parents also always end up needing to make appointments for me for doctors, dentists, hairdressers, etc that I haven’t been to before, which again, can be really frustrating. And I know this. I have days, weeks, or even months when I stop messaging people, even on goodreads, which I know is frustrating for my friends, but sometimes social interactions online become overwhelming when there’s so much going on in real life. I’m not about to sit here and pretend that my mental illnesses don’t sometimes make it more difficult to be around me or to know me. But I find that a lot of books about mental illness tend to skip over this aspect of it. And I know that some people may not be aware of it, but most people, at least in my experience, do know, to some extent, that it can be difficult to be friends with them because of their mental illness. And so the fact that this book brings this up is amazing, because it’s something that I always feel self-conscious about, or feel bad about. It can make you feel like a burden, sometimes, which is a hard feeling to get over. But, again, this book has managed to take one of my biggest insecurities and really show me that I’m not alone in feeling the way I do. And that really meant a lot to me.<br /><br />On top of the really good representation of anxiety through Norah’s thought patterns, Norah’s anxiety also manifests physically throughout this book, which is something that a lot of mental health books kind of forget about, so I really appreciated that aspect of the representation. Norah often wound her fingers into knots, sweat a lot, paced around the room, and picked at scabs or scratched herself in moments of anxiety.<br /><br />I especially loved the discussions Norah had with her psychiatrist about self harm. Because cutting wasn’t the only form of self harm that Norah partook in. Picking at scabs can be considered self harm (depending on the circumstances), as it’s interfering with the healing process. And scratching oneself is actually the most common form of self harm. Norah would do this when she was feeling very anxious to try to calm herself down by focusing on something other than whatever it was she was panicking about. In other words, she scratched herself and picked at scabs in an attempt to gain back control over herself as well. Sound familiar? Because of the intentions behind it, these things are considered self harm, and can be just as bad as cutting. (Disclaimer: please keep in mind that picking at a scab because you’re bored, or accidentally scratching your hand is <i>not</i> self harm. It’s both the physical act of harm <i>and</i> the intent behind it that makes an action self harm.)<br /><br />I really, really appreciated this discussion, because, as I said before, most people just think of cutting when they think of self harm, when it can actually be so much more than that. When I used to self harm, I wouldn’t just cut. I’d scratch my skin until it bled and would interfere with the healing process of cuts and scratches. I didn’t consider this self harm at the time, because it wasn’t cutting; it was just something I did to help me cope. It wasn’t until my psychologist at the time asked about a scar from a scratch that it was explained to me that this was also self harm. So I had a very similar experience to Norah regarding self harm, and so seeing someone else go through the same thing was really emotional, but also quite comforting, and I thought the scenes in this book that addressed this topic were just so raw and powerful.<br /><br />Beyond the mental health representation, I also just loved Norah as a character. She was self-aware, sarcastic, witty, very smart, and incredibly funny. Also, she acknowledged that she was pretty, but didn’t spend the entire book bragging about how gorgeous she was. She just overall had a personality. Like, outside of her mental illness. Which shouldn’t be something I feel like I have to praise authors for, but with the number of books I’ve read where the character with a mental illness is nothing but that mental illness, I feel like I kind of <i>have</i> to acknowledge that an author has done well in giving their character with a mental illness, you know, personality traits outside of their mental health. But yeah, I related to her in a lot of aspects, and I have a very similar sense of humour to her. Like, she had that sort of dry, I-hate-myself-but-can-laugh-about-it, morbid-at-times sort of sense of humour. I’m doing a shit job at explaining it, so here’s some examples (basically quoting the entire book at this point but oh well, I’m feeling lazy today):<br /><br /><i>“I twirl, because nothing says I’m mentally stable quite like an impromptu pirouette.”<br /><br />“The faint whistle of my plummeting school grades can be heard in the distance.”<br /><br />“The door clicks shut, and I wonder if I can buy a lobotomy on eBay.”<br /><br />“Why do people keep telling me to be myself? Honestly. It’s like they’ve never even met me.”<br /><br />“My self-esteem, already beaten black-and-blue, coughs up a lung.”</i><br /><br />Like, I get that maybe some people don’t find this kind of humour funny, but I absolutely love it.<br /><br />Ok, enough about Norah, I do want to talk about things other than the mental illness rep and my love for this books protagonist. Like the love interest for example. He was cute and sweet, but bland and underdeveloped, and I’ve completely forgotten his name because of that. (Just checked, his name is Luke.) Compared to the literal 5 pages of review I’ve just done focusing purely on Norah, you’d think I’d have more to say about Luke, but I honestly don’t. He was annoyingly perfect, to the point where it felt a little unrealistic, and he was also very forgettable, as he wasn’t really developed outside of his and Norah’s relationship. But, I did actually enjoy the romance. It was kind of instalovey, but still very cute, and I really enjoyed reading about Norah struggling to find where a romantic relationship fit into her overwhelming mental health journey, and Luke struggling to understand just how much Norah’s mental illnesses affected her. Overall, it was a much-needed fluffy aspect to an otherwise quite emotional book.<br /><br />However, their relationship wasn’t really the one that I LOVED. That would be Norah’s relationship with her mum (yes, m-u-m, you know, the British spelling, the way it <i>should have</i> been spelt in this <i>British</i> book (I’m sorry, I’m salty, I get enough American spelling in American books, I don’t need it in British ones too)). It was so emotional reading about Norah trying to become more independent and navigate her life and mental illnesses without her mum around 24/7, and seeing the struggles her mum had trying to take care of Norah whilst also doing the job she loved. Their dynamic was honestly so refreshingly real, and I loved reading about them. Some of their conversations were hilarious, whilst others were kind of heartbreaking, and a lot of aspects of their relationship reminded me of my relationship with my mum, so I really loved it. I would’ve liked to see a little more development for Norah’s mum, but all the characters that weren’t Norah were very underdeveloped, so it wasn’t just a problem with Norah’s mum specifically. I didn’t mind so much, though, because whilst the characters weren’t exactly developed individually, they were developed in regards to their relationship with Norah, which is what the book was really about, so it wasn’t a <i>huge</i> deal.<br /><br />Oh yay fun, I have, like, 500 characters left to talk about the plot, the writing, the tropes, and conclude this incoherent mess of a review. I love this character limit, it’s totally not restricting at all :)))<br /><br />Ok, the plot: this book was really about Norah learning to deal with her mental illnesses and navigate her relationships with the people in her life, and there wasn’t much of a plot outside of that. But I absolutely loved reading about Norah’s mental health struggles (Nahhh really? You did? Wow, nobody noticed) and seeing how that affected her relationships with the people in her life. I did find the book to be very predictable, though, which did hinder my enjoyment of it, and the ending was very abrupt. It kind of came out of nowhere, and then everything was suddenly over. <br /><br />I felt like, for the most part, the writing was fine. It wasn’t anything brilliant, and it was fairly simplistic, but it was certainly not terrible by any means, and it fit the story very well. However, the pacing was a bit off. And by a bit, I mean a lot. The story started off quite fast-paced, then slowed down, then the pacing bounced all over the place for a bit, found its rhythm, and then BAM! It finished. But, I was loving the story so much that the pacing issues didn’t really bother me <i>that</i>much.<br /><br />As for tropes, this book was a little cliche, which didn't help with the predictability, but it was full of tropes or anything. I’d rather talk about the tropes that this book <i>didn’t</i> have: there was no “the main character falls in love and her mental illness is miraculously cured” bs. Meeting Luke sparked a stronger desire within Norah to want to get better and be able to live her life more freely, but she still had her mental illness the entire time she was with him. By the end of the book, she was recovering, but was not at all recovered. And I loved that. There was also none of the “therapists suck” shit. Norah had a psychiatrist that she saw regularly who clearly cared about her and did her best to help her. And by the end of the story, Norah was even taking medication. Recovery processes were portrayed realistically, but positively within this book, and I loved it. There was no “this character has a mental illness, but it’s his/her entire personality because people with mental illnesses can’t be anything outside of them” bs or any “this character is supposed to have a mental illness, but that’s such a taboo subject that we’re just going to dance around that fact and never give them any sort of diagnosis” crap. There weren’t really any harmful mental illness tropes or stereotypes, and I loved it. As someone who suffers from mental illness, I felt so respected, because the author clearly did her best to put time and effort into respectfully and accurately portraying mental illness, and I’m so fucking here for it.<br /><br />Just a note: whilst the author did put mental health resources at the back of the book, there weren’t any trigger warnings (at least, none in the typical place, or that I could find anywhere else), which was a bit of a bummer. But I’m glad that she did at least offer mental health resources (though they were only for the UK, so it was still a bit limited if I’m honest).<br /><br />Ok, in conclusion, I am so fucking sorry if you’ve made it this far because damn this was a long one. I’ve literally cut so much out of this review, and it still barely fits within the character limit (mostly because I keep wasting characters talking about the character limit). But overall, the mental illness representation in this book was absolutely brilliant, and, me being me, I didn’t really care about much else. But, this book did have it’s issues, namely, the pacing, the instalove, the underdevelopment of the characters outside of Norah, the predictability, and the abrupt ending. However, if you’re partial to books about mental illness, I’d definitely pick this one up.<br /><br />(Also, I had to cut down on 15,000 characters. Please, Goodreads, I need more characters. This has been a PSA)</span>

<div id="review_1906459052" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1906459052" />
    <a title="Caitlin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/57334157-caitlin"><img alt="Caitlin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1507948675p2/57334157.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1906459052?book_show_action=true">Mar 17, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Caitlin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Caitlin" href="/user/show/57334157-caitlin">Caitlin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781910655863" href="/book/show/29566743-under-rose-tainted-skies">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/57334157-caitlin?shelf=2017-read">2017-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/57334157-caitlin?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/57334157-caitlin?shelf=4-stars">4-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/57334157-caitlin?shelf=anticipated-2017-release">anticipated-2017-release</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1906459052" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8461936057889028935">4.5 stars!<br/><br/><i>Trigger Warning: Self Harm</i><br/><br/><b>
  <i>"Mental health is usually the last place people go when they think about someone being sick.”</i>
</b><br/><br/>In general, I pretty much avoid contemporaries - especially those centred around mental health. I'm always incredibly worried that mental health would be treated inappropriately and really be more harmful than helpful. I originally heard about this book and how it dealt with similar topics like in <i>Everything, Everything</i> - which is not a good book in my opinion. I w</span>
  <span id="freeText8461936057889028935" style="display:none">4.5 stars!<br /><br /><i>Trigger Warning: Self Harm</i><br /><br /><b>
  <i>"Mental health is usually the last place people go when they think about someone being sick.”</i>
</b><br /><br />In general, I pretty much avoid contemporaries - especially those centred around mental health. I'm always incredibly worried that mental health would be treated inappropriately and really be more harmful than helpful. I originally heard about this book and how it dealt with similar topics like in <i>Everything, Everything</i> - which is not a good book in my opinion. I was pretty hesitant to want to read this book because of that fact, but <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1907073436?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Amber</a> then read it and really enjoyed it. My tastes are always pretty similar to Amber's and I know that if she recommends me a contemporary, there's a good reason behind it - especially since she knows I don't like many contemporaries. <br /><br />I went into this book with pretty low expectations and I was honestly shocked about how good this book was. It's real. It's raw. And most of all, it's important. It deals with serious topics such as agoraphobia, anxiety, OCD and self harm. I personally have a very limited understanding of agoraphobia (tbh I thought it was a fear of spiders) and reading a book about it <b>by an author who suffers from it</b> is incredibly refreshing. I feel like when mental health is concerned, you can't talk about it or do it justice unless you've suffered yourself. I found the OCD, anxiety and self harm aspects extremely realistic and there were so many scenes that I saw myself in Norah. I could completely relate to what she was dealing with and where her thought processes were coming through and it was honestly so refreshing. I hate when mental health is done incorrectly and this book just gives me so much hope for future books about mental health.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>"See, anxiety doesn't just stop. You can have nice moments, minutes where it shrinks, but it doesn't leave. It lurks in the background like a shadow, like that important assignment you have to do but keep putting off or the dull ache that follows a three-day migraine. The best you can hope for is to contain it, make it as small as possible so it stops being intrusive."</i>
</b><br /><br />Honestly, my favourite part was that, even though there was a love interest and a romantic plot, <b>love did not cure all</b>. Luke is an incredible love interest and is so supportive but he doesn't attempt to cure her. I can't even tell you how sick I am of books that deal with mental health being easily solved by love. <b>Love does not cure mental illnesses.</b> Sure, they can definitely help but they do not cure it. <br /><br /><b>
  <u>Mental health should never be used as a fun plot point that can be easily solved.</u>
</b> Norah is sick when we meet her and by the end, she is still sick but slowly recovering. <u>This is what it's really like.</u><br /><br />My favourite scene of the book is when Norah and her therapist discuss how Luke could react to her confessions about her mental health. I personally have had 2 different reactions (both good and bad) to sharing my mental health journey and it honestly still leaves me intimidated to share it with some people. Who knows what people's reactions are going to be? Some people are just completely unaccepting of mental health. When you tell someone you're sick, they expect you to say that you've got a broken bone or something along those lines, not that you're suffering from mental health problems. <br /><br />I'm sorry for the mess that is this review but I can't express enough how <b>IMPORTANT</b> this book is. I would recommend it to everyone. This is the type of mental health books we need. Please let 2017 be the end of 'love cures all problems' plot line.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8461936057889028935" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2183013536" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6308817617589517584">Find all of my reviews at: <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/'>http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/</a> <br/><br/><b>
  <i>“Why do people keep telling me to be myself? Honestly. It’s like they’ve never even met me.”</i>
</b><br/><br/>Every now and then a certain someone takes a break from training monkeys in order to send me little treasures I didn’t even know I wanted until I received them. <i>Under A Rose Tainted Sky</i> is one of those. When I received a message telling me I had some goodies waiting for me if I would get off airplane mode (said monkey trainer also has to ru</span>
  <span id="freeText6308817617589517584" style="display:none">Find all of my reviews at: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/">http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/</a> <br><br><b>
  <i>“Why do people keep telling me to be myself? Honestly. It’s like they’ve never even met me.”</i>
</b><br><br>Every now and then a certain someone takes a break from training monkeys in order to send me little treasures I didn’t even know I wanted until I received them. <i>Under A Rose Tainted Sky</i> is one of those. When I received a message telling me I had some goodies waiting for me if I would get off airplane mode (said monkey trainer also has to run interference in order to save me from my own stupid) I had much excite. Especially when I discovered this one was about someone with agoraphobia. Even my husband reacted like so when I told him what my book bestie had selected for me . . . . <br><br><a href="https://lunapic.com" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1511197372ra/24491190.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>What can I say????<br><br><a href="https://lunapic.com" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1511197372ra/24491191.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>So about the book. THIS is what that <i>Turtles <s>FUCKING SUCK!</s> All The Way Down</i> should have been. But NO. John Green will sell eleventy trillion copies of a giant pile of turtle suckage and this little gem will sell a handful. And don’t even give me the “John Green struggles with the same thing as his MC” argument, because THIS author does to. Now I’m going to let the book do the talking from here out so I don’t have an aneurysm. <br><br>Meet Norah – a 17-year old agoraphobic who leaves her house only to attend therapy. She is well aware that she needs to work on controlling her fears, else she . . . . <br><br><b>
  <i>“die cold and alone. Hidden in my room while strangers post messages of condolence on my social media and rabid cats eat my decomposing corpse.”</i>
</b><br><br>But managing her anxiety is easier said than done . . . . <br><br><b>
  <i> “Anxiety doesn’t just stop. You can have nice moments, minutes where it shrinks, but it doesn’t leave. It lurks in the background like a shadow, like that important assignment you have to do but keep putting off or the dull ache that follows a three-day migraine. The best you can hope for is to contain it, make it be as small as possible so it stops being intrusive.” </i>
</b><br><br>And when things get too overwhelming, sometimes she needs an escape . . . . <br><br><b>
  <i> “It’s drastic, a last resort. But so easy. Like breathing, blinking. One beat in time. One quick slice, where nobody can see, and it all stops. This is not about dying. This is about trying to get back some control.” </i>
</b><br><br>When Luke moves next door – and then continues to pop up on Norah’s front steps, laughing at her snarky commentary, withholding judgment regarding her lack of leaving the house – Norah is confronted with a new challenge . . . . <br><br><b>
  <i> “TV didn’t adequately prepare me for talking to boys in real life.” </i>
</b><br><br>Norah is well-aware her issues are quite the inhibitor when it comes to romance, but it doesn’t stop her from asking . . . . <br><br><b>
  <i> “Why can’t I be normal? Why can’t I think the way normal people do? I so desperately would have liked to have him as a friend.” </i>
</b><br><br>What Norah doesn’t realize is . . . . .<br><br><b>
  <i> “There isn’t much you miss when you’re really looking.”</i>
</b><br><br>If you want a different take on the “boy next door” story – this one might be a winner. I sure loved it . . . . <br><br><a href="https://lunapic.com" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1511197372ra/24491192.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a></span>

<div id="review_1774678793" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1774678793" />
    <a title="abby" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/44478099-abby"><img alt="abby" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1597252036p2/44478099.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1774678793?book_show_action=true">Dec 05, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="abby" class="user" itemprop="url" name="abby" href="/user/show/44478099-abby">abby</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44478099-abby?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44478099-abby?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44478099-abby?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44478099-abby?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44478099-abby?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1774678793" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3454168851107436832">2.5 stars. This one just didn't work for me.<br/><br/>Norah is agoraphobic, has OCD, and has not left her house in years apart from trips to the doctor. Her life is pretty much limited to what she can experience online. The only human being she has regular face to face contact with is her devoted and protective mother. Then a cute boy moves next door. For some reason, Luke finds Norah intriguing, if also a bit odd. They strike up a friendship of sorts, which mostly involves Norah staring at him through a </span>
  <span id="freeText3454168851107436832" style="display:none">2.5 stars. This one just didn't work for me.<br /><br />Norah is agoraphobic, has OCD, and has not left her house in years apart from trips to the doctor. Her life is pretty much limited to what she can experience online. The only human being she has regular face to face contact with is her devoted and protective mother. Then a cute boy moves next door. For some reason, Luke finds Norah intriguing, if also a bit odd. They strike up a friendship of sorts, which mostly involves Norah staring at him through a window, and then that grows into more as they get to know each other.<br /><br />I had real frustrations with this book. First, mostly nothing happened. Then there's the "love cures mental illness" thing. I don't think Luke ever <i>gets</i> it; he's always going on about what he and Norah will do "one day"-- that day being when his attention has cured her agoraphobia and they fly off to Paris together. To me, Luke and Norah's relationship was a perfect example of how sometimes a romance like this <b>can't work.</b> It would have been a bittersweet ending, but it would have been real. Instead, the author validates the "cute boy fixes brain" idea by showing that Norah does in fact start to improve because of Luke.<br /><br />I like Norah, and her relationship with her mother, but not much else. And the ending came out of left field and didn't fit with the rest of the book. Overall, I'm underwhelmed.<br /><br />I received a copy of this book courtesy of the publisher and NetGalley.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3454168851107436832" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1982779893" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1982779893" />
    <a title="Wren (fablesandwren)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/42780417-wren-fablesandwren"><img alt="Wren (fablesandwren)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596719528p2/42780417.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1982779893?book_show_action=true">Apr 26, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Wren (fablesandwren)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Wren (fablesandwren)" href="/user/show/42780417-wren-fablesandwren">Wren (fablesandwren)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42780417-wren-fablesandwren?shelf=03-stars">03-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42780417-wren-fablesandwren?shelf=not-shelved">not-shelved</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1982779893" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3458760441487191990">Overall, I really liked this story. <br/>I thought it was more realistic than other mental-illness based books that I have read.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1512866217ra/24639852.gif' alt='' width='350' height='144' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><u>Like</u>:<br/>001. That Norah, our main girl, knows that she is being irrational but also knows she has to do it that way or the world will implode.. irrationally. <br/>002. She calls herself crazy because, again, she knows that what she is doing is not necessary but at the same time it is necessary and she has to do it. Mental illness is weird. <br/>003. Luke, our main dude, reacts the same w</span>
  <span id="freeText3458760441487191990" style="display:none">Overall, I really liked this story. <br>I thought it was more realistic than other mental-illness based books that I have read.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1512866217ra/24639852.gif" alt="" width="350" height="144" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><u>Like</u>:<br>001. That Norah, our main girl, knows that she is being irrational but also knows she has to do it that way or the world will implode.. irrationally. <br>002. She calls herself crazy because, again, she knows that what she is doing is not necessary but at the same time it is necessary and she has to do it. Mental illness is weird. <br>003. Luke, our main dude, reacts the same way we would when Norah has an episode: wide-eyed, cautious and just wanting to help her get through whatever she is doing. <br>004. I really appreciated the fact that the boy didn't "cure" the girl. <b>That's my main enjoyment of this whole book</b>. Too many books have people being "cured" by getting in a relationship. That's not how life works. <br>005. I also really appreciated that it was more focused on her being able to do baby steps when she had companionship beyond her mother and her therapist. She can cope with the two women who have dedicated themselves to helping her, but she can slowly rewire herself the more helps she gets. That's important. As someone who deals with <b>
  <u>my own</u>
</b> type(s) of mental illness, it is so important to have a handful of people to keep you afloat. <br>006. The narrator, Pheobe Strole, did a phenomenal job.<br>007. The relationship between Norah and her mother was what touched my heart the most. I think it's because it reminded me of my relationship with my mother and I wanted to drive five hours to go give my mom a hug.<br><br><u>Didn't Like:</u><br>001. The writing was a little young for my taste, but it was still enjoyable. I think I would have rated it lower actually reading it; but Pheobe Strole did such a great job that it didn't bother me as much as it usually would have.<br><br>And the ending? My goodness, you do not expect something that insane to happen with such a happy-looking book. You don't expect your jaw to drop (yes, mine did physically drop) and go "is this really happening or is she imagining the absolute worst scenario?" It was happening. I died. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1512866217ra/24639853.gif" alt="" width="350" height="197" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Also, a little P.S. here: <i>You can't say things like "that's now how mental illness works" because all mental illnesses are different. Even if I had voices talking inside my head and you had voices talking inside your head, our likeness ends there. How I get better and how I deal is going to be different from how you get better and how you deal. <u>Individuality</u> people. It's a thing. Which is why you can't rationalize someone's anxiety just because you also deal with anxiety.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="3458760441487191990" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44487975-dannii-elle?shelf=contemporary-cuteness">contemporary-cuteness</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1945514691" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1020678459933950169">This is a heartbreaking and accurate account of a young life lived under the burden of mental illness. This is a must read for anyone looking to further their understanding of mental health and to read from more diverse perspectives. Despite the emotional nature of the tale, I found hope buried in the darkness and a reality that, however painful, was a necessary one to read about.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer2117444987" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10160898837422326121">I am not diagnosed with OCD or agoraphobia so I cannot comment on the representation but I enjoyed this a lot. :)</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_2147072521" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2147072521" />
    <a title="Beth" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/44125660-beth"><img alt="Beth" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1600268807p2/44125660.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2147072521?book_show_action=true">Oct 10, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Beth" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Beth" href="/user/show/44125660-beth">Beth</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781910655863" href="/book/show/29566743-under-rose-tainted-skies">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44125660-beth?shelf=2017-reads">2017-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44125660-beth?shelf=4-stars">4-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44125660-beth?shelf=stand-alone">stand-alone</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44125660-beth?shelf=mental-health">mental-health</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44125660-beth?shelf=my-heart-hurts">my-heart-hurts</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2147072521" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14566014254436871456"><b>4 Stars for Under Rose-Tainted Skies</b><br/><br/>Trigger Warning: Self Harm<br/><br/><i>"When people say "weird", what they really mean is "different". And difference has never been a bad thing" - Luke</i><br/><br/><b>This was everything.</b><br/><br/>Lately I've been wanting to read more books related to Mental Health and this has a few different factors which include: Agoraphobia, OCD, Anxiety and Depression. This may get slightly personal but sometimes I think it's good to speak about your own experiences and to know that you're not alone, I can't </span>
  <span id="freeText14566014254436871456" style="display:none"><b>4 Stars for Under Rose-Tainted Skies</b><br /><br />Trigger Warning: Self Harm<br /><br /><i>"When people say "weird", what they really mean is "different". And difference has never been a bad thing" - Luke</i><br /><br /><b>This was everything.</b><br /><br />Lately I've been wanting to read more books related to Mental Health and this has a few different factors which include: Agoraphobia, OCD, Anxiety and Depression. This may get slightly personal but sometimes I think it's good to speak about your own experiences and to know that you're not alone, I can't speak on behalf of all of these Mental Health areas but I can speak about my own experiences for a few. For roughly 10 years I've had Anxiety and Depression and the way in which it is described in this book was just so relatable. At times I found it difficult to leave my house, I suffered from Insomnia because of my anxiety. At times I hated myself and would often blame myself for what was happening and often felt alone and scared to speak out about it. Some thing really really struck home. Previously mentioned in one of my updates a character says to Norah "well you don't look ill" it's one of those things that you're like just because I don't look a certain way doesn't mean that something isn't happening. In the book, Dr Reeves puts it perfectly <i>"You don't expect anything, You talk, you teach"</i> I think what's make this book so much more is <b>that the author has actually dealt with this</b> and is therefore able to show what it's actually like.<br /><br />What I enjoyed is that in some books you can find that the MC gets a love interest and then suddenly their recovery is centred on this, this isn't the case for this book. Luke does support Norah but it's not as though he is there solely to make her get back to her "normal" self. It was just so refreshing to see and I really really appreciated this!<br /><br />I don't want to go too much into characters; we have Norah and her mum, Luke and Dr Reeves for the majority of the book. All for characters are so well done. I loved how patient Her mum, Dr Reeves and Luke were. My heart broke for Norah to know that at times she hated herself.<br /><br />What I <b>liked?</b><br />- How it just dealt with <u>everything</u>, the fact the Noarh knew she wasn't perfect was just so refreshing!<br />- LOTR reference!<br />- The cute little notes<br />- I loved Norahs mum!<br /><br />What I <b>didn't like?</b><br />- The ending seemed slightly rushed<br />- I don't know how to word this, the pacing seemed to be a bit all over the place...<br /><br />There were some really <u>really</u> important factors in this book, that I don't want to post as spoilers, this is definitely a book I'd recommend! Sorry if this review is a bit all over the place, it's difficult to review something like this when parts of the book can be so relatable, and others worlds apart. <br /><br /><i>See anxiety doesn't just stop. You can have nice moments, minutes where it shrinks, but it does't leave.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="14566014254436871456" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2114806637" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2114806637" />
    <a title="Hadya" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/55852574-hadya"><img alt="Hadya" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1586011465p2/55852574.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2114806637?book_show_action=true">Sep 06, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Hadya" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Hadya" href="/user/show/55852574-hadya">Hadya</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2114806637" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1267567128367605317"><b> 5 stars <br/><i> Since I'm the laziest person you'll meet this is the same review as the one on my blog lol </i> </b><br/>This book was the best Mental Health representation I have ever read.<br/><br/>Louise Gornall manages to paint such a vivid image in our mind about what Norah goes through, and how a person who has Agoraphobia’s mind works. I realize that people without the illness can never realize the full extent of it, of how it works, and we can’t even pretend to understand it, but the way Louise Gornall wrote this bo</span>
  <span id="freeText1267567128367605317" style="display:none"><b> 5 stars <br /><i> Since I'm the laziest person you'll meet this is the same review as the one on my blog lol </i> </b><br />This book was the best Mental Health representation I have ever read.<br /><br />Louise Gornall manages to paint such a vivid image in our mind about what Norah goes through, and how a person who has Agoraphobia’s mind works. I realize that people without the illness can never realize the full extent of it, of how it works, and we can’t even pretend to understand it, but the way Louise Gornall wrote this book, the way she describes it, and her writing style and depth in the illness, makes me believe for the period I am reading this book, that I am Norah.<br /><br />The synopsis is painted out to be a normal romance contemporary novel, and how love overcomes mental illness, but it’s nothing like that. Love does not overcome mental illness, just because you meet someone who you love, doesnt mean your illness decides to say “Oh okay this person found love, time for me to leave now.” No, this book is about how Norah learns how to deal with her illness, with a short love story in the side. By the end of the book Norah doesn’t “get rid of” her illness, no, she still has it, but she’s trying to learn how to deal with it.<br /><br />The mother daughter relationship in this was perfection. I absolutely loved how close Norah and her mom are, it was a breath of fresh air after the whole “parents don’t understand anything” teenager cliche trope that goes around in most contemporaries.<br /><br />And this is actually the first time I have read a therapist relationship where the person, receives comfort and solace from their therapist, instead of hating their guts and wishing they could shut up, and I loved it.<br /><br />There was nothing in this book that I disliked or hated, I loved everything. I loved the way everything was described, how the characters were, the romance, the representation.<br /><br />This book is super short if you want to read it and I’d highly recommend it to everyone.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1267567128367605317" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer16959245851200945319">So I read this literally ages ago and I remember nothing from it, so here’s a quick short list review for finally get this RTC out of the way!!<br/><br/>- <b>There was amazing mental illness rep</b> (including anxiety, agoraphobia, and OCD, I believe), according to a few ownvoices reviews. I don’t remember exactly how Nora’s anxiety was portrayed, but, saying this as a person with anxiety, I think it was written realistically! The book is also ownvoices as well.<br/>- <b>Nora was a really beautiful character</b>, and her th</span>
  <span id="freeText16959245851200945319" style="display:none">So I read this literally ages ago and I remember nothing from it, so here’s a quick short list review for finally get this RTC out of the way!!<br /><br />- <b>There was amazing mental illness rep</b> (including anxiety, agoraphobia, and OCD, I believe), according to a few ownvoices reviews. I don’t remember exactly how Nora’s anxiety was portrayed, but, saying this as a person with anxiety, I think it was written realistically! The book is also ownvoices as well.<br />- <b>Nora was a really beautiful character</b>, and her thoughts were so real and often relatable. She was so well-developed and it was great to see her grow and try to recover throughout the book.<br />I also LOVED LUKE a lot. He was such a sweet boy who genuinely cared for Nora and he’s just super lovable.<br />- I THINK that the romance was a slowburn?? Or friends to lovers?? Or at least something with amazing development? And it didn’t play into the “love cures all” trope, which is really important when there’s romance in a book about mental illness.<br />- The romance was also just so so cute. God. I think I smiled way too much while reading this book.<br />- Despite it being cute and all, <b>it actually made my heart break a few times</b>. I love the way mental health was tackled and certain scenes were so sad to read about. <br />- I mean, I don’t remember the scenes, but according to my notes that I took after reading this, I was apparently sad…<br />- Basically, this was very cute but also very heartbreaking, in a perfect balance. And it had great characters with a well-developed romance, as well as a great portrayal of mental illness!</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer9348006062331398098">Oh gosh this book brought tears to my eyes! It's a short story on an important matter that affects millions of people in our everyday lives. The core of this book is about how the main character, Norah copes with having agoraphobia, anxiety, and OCD. It's not an easy subject to talk about but I think the author did an incredible job to evoke the struggles and triumphs that her character faced. I found myself crying one minute to laughing in the next while also rooting for her, all along. There i</span>
  <span id="freeText9348006062331398098" style="display:none">Oh gosh this book brought tears to my eyes! It's a short story on an important matter that affects millions of people in our everyday lives. The core of this book is about how the main character, Norah copes with having agoraphobia, anxiety, and OCD. It's not an easy subject to talk about but I think the author did an incredible job to evoke the struggles and triumphs that her character faced. I found myself crying one minute to laughing in the next while also rooting for her, all along. There is also a romantic interest involved that felt so real and beautiful, I highly recommend giving this book a try! :) </span>

<div id="review_2748141720" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2748141720" />
    <a title="Katie Gallagher" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/79865972-katie-gallagher"><img alt="Katie Gallagher" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1557351146p2/79865972.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2748141720?book_show_action=true">Apr 22, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katie Gallagher" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katie Gallagher" href="/user/show/79865972-katie-gallagher">Katie Gallagher</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2748141720" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15568048997395538664"><a href='https://katiejgallagher.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <i>Read this review and others on my blog!</i>
</a><br/><br/>I read pretty much exclusively fiction, but even so, a good majority of the books I read are for research purposes, with the aim of informing and improving my writing. I might pick up a book that I think would be a good comp title, reread a book to study an author's voice or methods for conjuring a specific mood, or even read a new release just to stay in touch with current literary trends. All this is why I basically abandoned reading fantasy last year</span>
  <span id="freeText15568048997395538664" style="display:none"><a href="https://katiejgallagher.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <i>Read this review and others on my blog!</i>
</a><br /><br />I read pretty much exclusively fiction, but even so, a good majority of the books I read are for research purposes, with the aim of informing and improving my writing. I might pick up a book that I think would be a good comp title, reread a book to study an author's voice or methods for conjuring a specific mood, or even read a new release just to stay in touch with current literary trends. All this is why I basically abandoned reading fantasy last year—I just had a lot of books to read for research, the majority of them great, but none of them fantasy.<br /><br />So it was for research purposes that Louise Gornall's <i>Under Rose-Tainted Skies</i> came onto my radar. I was considering including a character with agoraphobia in my new "Beauty and the Beast and aliens" WIP, so I wanted to get a sense of how this condition is tackled in fiction, especially in YA fiction. Gornall herself drew on her own experience and struggles in writing this book, and it shows—there is nothing in this book that is not raw and authentic. I read it in less than twenty-four hours—simply could not put it down. The MC is absolutely compelling, a character you can't help but root for as she deals with OCD, anxiety, and agoraphobia, all while building a relationship with the handsome, awkward boy next door who sees past her mental health struggles. Voice is everything in this book, and Gornall lets us stay tapped into the MC's thoughts like we're a neuron in her brain. She's flawed, funny, likable, and, above all, real. You can see how she comes to have the thought patterns she does—I found this fascinating, especially because I recognized some of my own unhealthy thought patterns taken to the next level by the MC. It really gave me pause and helped me examine my own headspace.<br /><br />You might be wondering if a book spent pretty much entirely in the MC's house would grow stale, but nothing here is boring. In fact, this is one of those rare reads where I finished it and felt that sad, lonely ache, where you just want to go back to page one and start the story over again. Suffice it to say that this is a five star read.<br /><br />I also want to briefly laud the author's treatment of the MC's relationship with her mother. I adore realistic parents in YA, and the relationship here was just perfect—nothing forced or scripted.<br /><br />In the end, I did make the decision that an agoraphobic character isn't the right fit for my book. Anxiety or OCD might make an appearance, not sure yet, but definitely not agoraphobia. And I am so happy to have been able to read this book to make an informed decision about that. I will absolutely be picking up future works by this author, and I recommend <i>Under Rose-Tainted Skies</i> for... everyone! Everyone should read this book! Right now!</span>
  <a data-text-id="15568048997395538664" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1857958687" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1857958687" />
    <a title="Chelsea slytherink" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/33481873-chelsea-slytherink"><img alt="Chelsea slytherink" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1550223913p2/33481873.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1857958687?book_show_action=true">Feb 19, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chelsea slytherink" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chelsea slytherink" href="/user/show/33481873-chelsea-slytherink">Chelsea slytherink</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33481873-chelsea-slytherink?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33481873-chelsea-slytherink?shelf=read-in-2017">read-in-2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33481873-chelsea-slytherink?shelf=representation-disability">representation-disability</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1857958687" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13917669628496498366">review also posted on <a href='http://romweasley.wordpress.com/2017/02/27/under-rose-tainted-skies-an-enjoyable-ownvoices-story/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Wordpress!</a> spoiler-free review!<br/><br/><blockquote>"I've heard <i>You don't look mentally ill</i> at least a half a dozen times in the past four years, a couple of those times from my former friends. I blame the media, stereotyping "mental illness" and calling every murderer since Manson crazy. People always seem to be expecting wide eyes and a kitchen knife dripping with blood."</blockquote><br/><br/><i>Under Rose-Tainted Skies</i> is about a girl named Norah who struggles with agoraphobia and OCD. The premise of this is similar</span>
  <span id="freeText13917669628496498366" style="display:none">review also posted on <a href="http://romweasley.wordpress.com/2017/02/27/under-rose-tainted-skies-an-enjoyable-ownvoices-story/" rel="nofollow noopener">Wordpress!</a> spoiler-free review!<br /><br /><blockquote>"I've heard <i>You don't look mentally ill</i> at least a half a dozen times in the past four years, a couple of those times from my former friends. I blame the media, stereotyping "mental illness" and calling every murderer since Manson crazy. People always seem to be expecting wide eyes and a kitchen knife dripping with blood."</blockquote><br /><br /><i>Under Rose-Tainted Skies</i> is about a girl named Norah who struggles with agoraphobia and OCD. The premise of this is similar to <i>Everything, Everything</i> by Nicola Yoon, but without the ableist representation (you can find more information about that <a href="http://disabilityinkidlit.com/2015/09/04/review-everything-everything-by-nicola-yoon/&lt;br /&gt;" rel="nofollow noopener">here</a>). This book is an <b>#ownvoices</b> story because Louise Gornall, the author, is also agoraphobic. Two reviewers who struggle with mental illnesses similar to Norah's agree that the representation is accurate (as you can read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1648291370?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">here</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1636333905?book_show_action=true&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">here</a>).<br /><br />This book also deals with <b>self-harm, eating disorders and depression</b>, so be aware of that in case that triggers you. I did find the descriptions of self-harm and fainting relatable. <br /><br />Unfortunately, that wasn't enough for me to love this. <b>Contemporary romances are not my favourites and <i>Under Rose-Tainted Skies</i> is no exception. Thankfully, however, there was no instalove and mental illness isn't "cured" once the characters fall in love.</b><br /><br />Furthermore, I didn't love the writing style. Because of Norah's mental illness, she gets distracted easily during conversations. Which interrupted the conversations quite often. While I completely understand why the author did that, it wasn't enjoyable to read. Once I finished a chapter, I put the book down for several minutes. <b>This book just couldn't keep me intrigued.</b> I also spotted some spelling mistakes and things didn't add up. Luke's phone was being fixed, yet he was using his phone to talk to someone. This didn't cause any major problems while reading, but I did find it annoying because it occurred more than once. <br /><br />My main complaint has to be the <b>lack of female friendships</b>. Girls are called "chicks" multiple times and Amy, the only female character we learn about besides Norah's mother, is basically described as a rich, blonde, popular bimbo. Naturally I understand that Norah doesn't allow a lot of people in her life, but I would think that the internet could be a solution for that. If she were to make friends with people online, perhaps that wouldn't trigger her agoraphobia. <br /><br />Even though I didn't love this book, I'm thankful it exists. The quote I used at the beginning proves there are stigmas of mental illness, so <b>it is important that books represent it in an accurate way. Still, I wish more books focussed on recovery instead of primarily the struggles that are caused by a mental illness.</b> Books like <i>Under Rose-Tainted Skies</i> end on a positive note, but the rest of the book is filled with anxiety, depression, etc. Which is okay, because those stories have to be told, but I wish there were as many books out there that focus on recovery. I'd for instance rather read a book about someone who is recovering from anorexia than someone who struggles with it throughout a book and only seeks help at the end.<br /><br /><b>conclusion:</b> <i>Under Rose-Tainted Skies</i> is an enjoyable read. I would definitely recommend it to anyone with mental illnesses or people who want to read an accurate portrayal of one. <br /><br />✿ You can also find me on <a href="http://twitter.com/romweasleys" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a>, <a href="http://www.instagram.com/romweasley/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a>, <a href="http://romweasleybooks.tumblr.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Tumblr</a>, <a href="https://nl.pinterest.com/romweasley/" rel="nofollow noopener">Pinterest</a> and <a href="http://romweasley.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Wordpress</a>! ✿</span>
  <a data-text-id="13917669628496498366" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('H6adgf5v4C/rj8vZaN1W4pCSHfCoTY15ylFRbVjRw+R/cvPjaeA8Glvg3lGUnu2IrT7jc1uHwDXrpisJox01vw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('NM8wR1lmKIYU1T+G68X9v3yK/qdRzTw7pGGyDmQPcVhUG14lzun0s6S6Kg4XhkbVQSYAJKIHcXeFlshqn8OHAw==')})
  }
